/ &#xfeff;</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">51.53000°N 0.12528°W</span><span style="display:none">&#xfeff; / <span class="geo">51.53000; -0.12528</span></span></span></a></span></span></span></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><a href="/wiki/File:Underground_sign_at_Westminster.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Underground sign at Westminster.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Underground_sign_at_Westminster.jpg/16px-Underground_sign_at_Westminster.jpg" decoding="async" width="16" height="15" class="noviewer" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Underground_sign_at_Westminster.jpg/24px-Underground_sign_at_Westminster.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Underground_sign_at_Westminster.jpg/32px-Underground_sign_at_Westminster.jpg 2x" data-file-width="820" data-file-height="750" /></a> <a href="/wiki/Portal:London_transport" title="Portal:London transport">London transport&#32;portal</a></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>St Pancras railway station</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;p&#39; in &#39;pie&#39;">p</span><span title="/æ/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;bad&#39;">æ</span><span title="/ŋ/: &#39;ng&#39; in &#39;sing&#39;">ŋ</span><span title="&#39;k&#39; in &#39;kind&#39;">k</span><span title="&#39;r&#39; in &#39;rye&#39;">r</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span><span title="&#39;s&#39; in &#39;sigh&#39;">s</span></span>/</a></span></span>), also known as <b>London St Pancras</b> and officially since 2007 as <b>St Pancras International</b>, is a <a href="/wiki/London_station_group" title="London station group">central London railway terminus</a> on <a href="/wiki/Euston_Road" title="Euston Road">Euston Road</a> in the <a href="/wiki/London_Borough_of_Camden" title="London Borough of Camden">London Borough of Camden</a>. It is the terminus for <a href="/wiki/Eurostar" title="Eurostar">Eurostar</a> continental services from London via <a href="/wiki/High_Speed_1" title="High Speed 1">High Speed 1</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Channel_Tunnel" title="Channel Tunnel">Channel Tunnel</a> to Belgium, France and the Netherlands. It provides <a href="/wiki/East_Midlands_Railway" title="East Midlands Railway">East Midlands Railway</a> services to <a href="/wiki/Corby_railway_station" title="Corby railway station">Corby</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Sheffield railway station">Sheffield</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nottingham_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Nottingham railway station">Nottingham</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Midland_Main_Line" title="Midland Main Line">Midland Main Line</a>, <a href="/wiki/Southeastern_(train_operating_company)" title="Southeastern (train operating company)">Southeastern</a> high-speed trains to <a href="/wiki/Kent" title="Kent">Kent</a> via <a href="/wiki/Ebbsfleet_International_railway_station" title="Ebbsfleet International railway station">Ebbsfleet International</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ashford_International_railway_station" title="Ashford International railway station">Ashford International</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Thameslink_(route)" class="mw-redirect" title="Thameslink (route)">Thameslink</a> cross-London services to <a href="/wiki/Bedford" title="Bedford">Bedford</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peterborough" title="Peterborough">Peterborough</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brighton" title="Brighton">Brighton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gatwick_Airport" title="Gatwick Airport">Gatwick Airport</a>. It stands between the <a href="/wiki/British_Library" title="British Library">British Library</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Regent%27s_Canal" title="Regent&#39;s Canal">Regent's Canal</a> and <a href="/wiki/London_King%27s_Cross_railway_station" title="London King&#39;s Cross railway station">King's Cross railway station</a>, with which it shares a <a href="/wiki/London_Underground" title="London Underground">London Underground</a> station, <a href="/wiki/King%27s_Cross_St._Pancras_tube_station" class="mw-redirect" title="King&#39;s Cross St. Pancras tube station">King's Cross St. Pancras</a>.
</p><p>The station was constructed by the <a href="/wiki/Midland_Railway" title="Midland Railway">Midland Railway</a> (MR), which had an extensive network across the Midlands and the North of England, but no dedicated line into London. After rail traffic problems following the <a href="/wiki/1862_International_Exhibition" title="1862 International Exhibition">1862 International Exhibition</a>, the MR decided to build a connection from Bedford to London with their own terminus. The station was designed by <a href="/wiki/William_Henry_Barlow" title="William Henry Barlow">William Henry Barlow</a> and constructed with a single-span iron roof. Following the station's opening on 1 October 1868, the MR constructed the <a href="/wiki/Midland_Grand_Hotel" class="mw-redirect" title="Midland Grand Hotel">Midland Grand Hotel</a> on the station's façade, which has been widely praised for its architecture and is now a Grade&#160;I <a href="/wiki/Listed_building" title="Listed building">listed building</a> along with the rest of the station.
</p><p>By the 1960s, St Pancras was surplus to requirements and services were diverted to King's Cross and <a href="/wiki/Euston_railway_station" title="Euston railway station">Euston</a> but there was fierce opposition to its proposed closure and demolition of the station and hotel. The station was reinvented in the late 20th century as the terminal for the <a href="/wiki/Channel_Tunnel_Rail_Link" class="mw-redirect" title="Channel Tunnel Rail Link">Channel Tunnel Rail Link</a> in an <a href="/wiki/Urban_regeneration" class="mw-redirect" title="Urban regeneration">urban regeneration</a> plan across East London. The complex underwent a £800&#160;million refurbishment which was opened by Queen <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Elizabeth II</a> in November 2007. A security-sealed terminal area was constructed for Eurostar services to <a href="/wiki/Continental_Europe" title="Continental Europe">continental Europe</a> via High Speed 1 and the Channel Tunnel, with platforms for domestic trains to the north and south-east of England. The restored station has 15 platforms, a shopping centre, and a coach facility. St Pancras is owned by <a href="/wiki/London_and_Continental_Railways" title="London and Continental Railways">London and Continental Railways</a> (LCR) and managed by Network Rail (High Speed), a subsidiary of <a href="/wiki/Network_Rail" title="Network Rail">Network Rail</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Location">Location</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St_Pancras_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Location">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>St Pancras is at the southern end of the <a href="/wiki/London_Borough_of_Camden" title="London Borough of Camden">London Borough of Camden</a> on a site orientated north/south, deeper than it is wide. The south is bounded by <a href="/wiki/Euston_Road" title="Euston Road">Euston Road</a> (part of the <a href="/wiki/London_Inner_Ring_Road" title="London Inner Ring Road">London Inner Ring Road</a>), and its frontage is the St Pancras Renaissance Hotel, while the west is bounded by Midland Road which separates it from the <a href="/wiki/British_Library" title="British Library">British Library</a> and the east by Pancras Road which separates it from <a href="/wiki/London_King%27s_Cross_railway_station" title="London King&#39;s Cross railway station">King's Cross station</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NHLE_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NHLE-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> The British Library is on the former goods yard site.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Behind the hotel, the train shed is elevated 5&#160;m (17&#160;ft) above street level and the area below forms the station <a href="/wiki/Undercroft" title="Undercroft">undercroft</a>. The northern half of the station is mainly bounded to the east by Camley Street, with Camley Street Natural Park across the road. To the north-east is <a href="/wiki/King%27s_Cross_Central" title="King&#39;s Cross Central">King's Cross Central</a>, formerly known as the Railway Lands, a complex of intersecting railway lines crossed by several roads and the <a href="/wiki/Regent%27s_Canal" title="Regent&#39;s Canal">Regent's Canal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-stsgsp_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stsgsp-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mrspi_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mrspi-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Several London bus routes serve St Pancras, including 10, 59, 73, 205 and 390.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St_Pancras_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St_Pancras_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:St_Pancras_station_train_shed_under_construction_in_1868_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/St_Pancras_station_train_shed_under_construction_in_1868_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-St_Pancras_station_train_shed_under_construction_in_1868_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/St_Pancras_station_train_shed_under_construction_in_1868_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-St_Pancras_station_train_shed_under_construction_in_1868_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/St_Pancras_station_train_shed_under_construction_in_1868_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-St_Pancras_station_train_shed_under_construction_in_1868_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4070" data-file-height="2805" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:St_Pancras_station_train_shed_under_construction_in_1868_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The train shed under construction in 1868</div></div></div>
<p>The station's name comes from the <a href="/wiki/St_Pancras,_London" title="St Pancras, London">St. Pancras</a> neighbourhood, which originates from the fourth-century Christian boy martyr <a href="/wiki/Pancras_of_Rome" title="Pancras of Rome">Pancras of Rome</a>. The station was commissioned by the <a href="/wiki/Midland_Railway" title="Midland Railway">Midland Railway</a> (MR), who had a network of routes in the Midlands, and in south and west Yorkshire and Lancashire but no route of its own to London. Before 1857 the MR used the lines of the L&amp;NWR for trains into the capital; subsequently the company's <a href="/wiki/Leicester_and_Hitchin_Railway" class="mw-redirect" title="Leicester and Hitchin Railway">Leicester and Hitchin Railway</a> gave access to London via the <a href="/wiki/Great_Northern_Railway_(Great_Britain)" title="Great Northern Railway (Great Britain)">Great Northern Railway</a> (GNR).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarlow187078_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarlow187078-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1862, traffic for the second <a href="/wiki/1862_International_Exhibition" title="1862 International Exhibition">International Exhibition</a> suffered extensive delays over the stretch of line into London over the GNR's track; the route into the city via the L&amp;NWR was also at capacity, with coal trains causing the network at <a href="/wiki/Rugby_railway_station" title="Rugby railway station">Rugby</a> and elsewhere to reach effective gridlock.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJackson198459–60_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJackson198459–60-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> This was the stimulus for the MR to build its own line to London from Bedford,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilliams1888128–29_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilliams1888128–29-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> which would be just under 50 miles (80&#160;km) long.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJackson198460_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJackson198460-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Carter_(Coventry_MP)" title="Samuel Carter (Coventry MP)">Samuel Carter</a> was solicitor for the parliamentary bill, which was sanctioned in 1863.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Design_and_construction">Design and construction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St_Pancras_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Design and construction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:St_Pancras_Station.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/St_Pancras_Station.png/220px-St_Pancras_Station.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="128" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/St_Pancras_Station.png/330px-St_Pancras_Station.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/St_Pancras_Station.png/440px-St_Pancras_Station.png 2x" data-file-width="1336" data-file-height="778" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:St_Pancras_Station.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The interior of the Barlow Trainshed, circa 1870</div></div></div>
<p>The station was designed by <a href="/wiki/William_Henry_Barlow" title="William Henry Barlow">William Henry Barlow</a> and constructed on a site that had previously been a slum called <a href="/wiki/Agar_Town" title="Agar Town">Agar Town</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWeinrebHibbertKeayKeay2008804_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeinrebHibbertKeayKeay2008804-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-thpan_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thpan-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Though coal and goods were the main motivation to build the station, the Midland realised the prestige of having a central London terminus, and decided it must have a front on Euston Road. The company purchased the eastern section of land on the road's north side owned by <a href="/wiki/Charles_Somers-Cocks,_3rd_Earl_Somers" title="Charles Somers-Cocks, 3rd Earl Somers">Earl Somers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJackson198460_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJackson198460-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:DISTRICT(1888)_p137_-_St_Pancras_Station_(plan).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/DISTRICT%281888%29_p137_-_St_Pancras_Station_%28plan%29.jpg/170px-DISTRICT%281888%29_p137_-_St_Pancras_Station_%28plan%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="277" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/DISTRICT%281888%29_p137_-_St_Pancras_Station_%28plan%29.jpg/255px-DISTRICT%281888%29_p137_-_St_Pancras_Station_%28plan%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/DISTRICT%281888%29_p137_-_St_Pancras_Station_%28plan%29.jpg/340px-DISTRICT%281888%29_p137_-_St_Pancras_Station_%28plan%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="789" data-file-height="1287" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:DISTRICT(1888)_p137_-_St_Pancras_Station_(plan).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Plan of St Pancras in 1888</div></div></div>
<p>The approaching line to the station crossed the Regent's Canal at height allowing the line reasonable gradients; this resulted in the level of the line at St Pancras being 20&#160;ft (6.1&#160;m) above the ground level.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJackson198460_16-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJackson198460-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Initial plans were for a two or three span roof with the void between station and ground level filled with spoil from tunnelling to join the Midland Main Line to the St. Pancras branch.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJackson198461_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJackson198461-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Instead, due to the value of the land in such a location the lower area was used for freight, in particular <a href="/wiki/Brewers_of_Burton" title="Brewers of Burton">beer from Burton</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJackson198462_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJackson198462-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;a&#93;</a></sup> As a result, the undercroft was built with columns and girders, maximising space, set out to the same plans as those used for beer warehouses, and with a basic unit of length that of a beer barrel.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarlow187079–80_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarlow187079–80-24">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The contract for the construction of the station substructure and connecting lines was given to <a href="/wiki/Waring_Brothers" title="Waring Brothers">Messrs. Waring</a>, with Barlow's assistant Campion as supervisor.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarlow187082_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarlow187082-25">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> The lower floor for beer warehousing contained interior columns 15&#160;ft (4.57&#160;m) wide, and 48&#160;ft (14.63&#160;m) deep carrying girders supporting the main station and track.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarlow187083Description_of_the_Lower_Floor_(Plate_9)_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarlow187083Description_of_the_Lower_Floor_(Plate_9)-26">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> The connection to the Widened Lines (St. Pancras branch) ran below the station's bottom level, in an east-to-west direction.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarlow187082_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarlow187082-25">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>To avoid the foundations of the roof interfering with the space beneath, and to simplify the design, and minimise cost, it was decided to construct a single span roof, with cross ties for the arch at the station level. The arch was sprung directly from the station level, with no piers.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarlow187080–81_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarlow187080–81-27">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJackson198462_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJackson198462-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Additional advice on the design of the roof was given to Barlow by <a href="/wiki/Rowland_Mason_Ordish" title="Rowland Mason Ordish">Rowland Mason Ordish</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarlow187082_25-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarlow187082-25">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> The arches' ribs had a web depth of 6&#160;ft (1.8&#160;m), mostly open ironwork. The span width, from wall to wall was 245&#160;ft 6&#160;in (74.83&#160;m), with a rib every 29&#160;ft 4&#160;in (8.94&#160;m) The arch was a slightly pointed design, with a reduced <a href="/wiki/Radius_of_curvature_(mathematics)" class="mw-redirect" title="Radius of curvature (mathematics)">radius of curvature</a> at the springing points. The <a href="/wiki/Butterley_Company" title="Butterley Company">Butterley Company</a> was contracted to construct the arches.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarlow187083–85Description_of_the_Roof_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarlow187083–85Description_of_the_Roof-28">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> The total cost of the 24 rib roof and glazing was over £53,000, of which over half was for the main ribs. The cost of the gable end was a further £8,500.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarlow187088–89Cost_of_the_Roof_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarlow187088–89Cost_of_the_Roof-29">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:St_Pancras_Clock.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/St_Pancras_Clock.jpg/170px-St_Pancras_Clock.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/St_Pancras_Clock.jpg/255px-St_Pancras_Clock.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/St_Pancras_Clock.jpg/340px-St_Pancras_Clock.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2448" data-file-height="3264" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:St_Pancras_Clock.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The clock tower of St Pancras</div></div></div>
<p>The single-span overall roof was the largest such structure in the world at the time of its completion.<sup id="cite_ref-thpan_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thpan-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> The materials used were <a href="/wiki/Wrought_iron" title="Wrought iron">wrought iron</a> framework of <a href="/wiki/Latticework" title="Latticework">lattice</a> design, with glass covering the middle half and timber (inside)/slate (outside) covering the outer quarters. The two end screens were glazed in a vertical rectangular grid pattern with decorative timber cladding around the edge and wrought iron <a href="/wiki/Finials" class="mw-redirect" title="Finials">finials</a> around the outer edge. It was 689 feet (210.01&#160;m) long, 240 feet (73.15&#160;m) wide, and 100 feet (30.48&#160;m) high at the apex above the tracks.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJackson198462_21-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJackson198462-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMason20167_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMason20167-30">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> At the time of opening, it was the world's largest unsupported station roof.<sup id="cite_ref-NHLE_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NHLE-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Local services began running to the <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Railway" title="Metropolitan Railway">Metropolitan Railway</a> junction underneath the terminus on 13 July 1868. The station itself opened to the public on 1 October. The first service was an overnight mail train from Leeds.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJackson198466_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJackson198466-31">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChristopher201311_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChristopher201311-32">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_services">Early services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St_Pancras_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Early services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>St Pancras was built during a period of expansion for the MR, as the major routes to Manchester, Nottingham, Sheffield and Carlisle opened during this time. By 1902, there were 150 trains arriving and leaving the station daily, though this figure was far less than Waterloo or Liverpool Street. As well as Midland services, the <a href="/wiki/Great_Eastern_Railway" title="Great Eastern Railway">Great Eastern Railway</a> (GER) used St Pancras as a "<a href="/wiki/West_End_of_London" title="West End of London">West End</a>" terminus for trains to <a href="/wiki/Great_Yarmouth_railway_station" title="Great Yarmouth railway station">Great Yarmouth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Norwich_railway_station" title="Norwich railway station">Norwich</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lowestoft_railway_station" title="Lowestoft railway station">Lowestoft</a> between 1870 and 1917. At the turn of the 20th century, St Pancras also had a faster service to <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_railway_station" title="Cambridge railway station">Cambridge</a> than King's Cross, at 71 minutes. GER services were suspended because of World War I and never resumed.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJackson198471_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJackson198471-33">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/London,_Tilbury_and_Southend_Railway" title="London, Tilbury and Southend Railway">London, Tilbury and Southend Railway</a> (LTSR) began offering <a href="/wiki/Boat_train" title="Boat train">boat train</a> services from St Pancras from 9 July 1894, following the opening of the <a href="/wiki/Tottenham_and_Forest_Gate_Railway" title="Tottenham and Forest Gate Railway">Tottenham and Forest Gate Railway</a>. The trains ran from St Pancras to <a href="/wiki/Tilbury_Riverside_railway_station" title="Tilbury Riverside railway station">Tilbury</a> via <a href="/wiki/South_Tottenham_railway_station" title="South Tottenham railway station">South Tottenham</a> and <a href="/wiki/Barking_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Barking railway station">Barking</a>. <a href="/wiki/Tilbury_Docks" class="mw-redirect" title="Tilbury Docks">Tilbury Docks</a> then provided a connection to Australia and Scandinavia. The following year, the LTSR began a service from St Pancras to <a href="/wiki/Southend_Central_railway_station" title="Southend Central railway station">Southend Central</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJackson198471_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJackson198471-33">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Boat trains continued to run from St Pancras until 1963, after which they were moved to Liverpool Street and Fenchurch Street.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJackson198472_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJackson198472-34">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Grouping.2C_nationalisation_and_privatisation"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Grouping,_nationalisation_and_privatisation">Grouping, nationalisation and privatisation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St_Pancras_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Grouping, nationalisation and privatisation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:St_Pancras_railway_station_bomb_damage_in_May_1941.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/St_Pancras_railway_station_bomb_damage_in_May_1941.jpg/220px-St_Pancras_railway_station_bomb_damage_in_May_1941.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/St_Pancras_railway_station_bomb_damage_in_May_1941.jpg/330px-St_Pancras_railway_station_bomb_damage_in_May_1941.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/St_Pancras_railway_station_bomb_damage_in_May_1941.jpg/440px-St_Pancras_railway_station_bomb_damage_in_May_1941.jpg 2x" data-file-width="692" data-file-height="523" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:St_Pancras_railway_station_bomb_damage_in_May_1941.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The station was damaged by a bomb in May 1941 during <a href="/wiki/The_Blitz" title="The Blitz">the Blitz</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Railways_Act_1921" title="Railways Act 1921">Railways Act of 1921</a> forced the merger of the Midland with the <a href="/wiki/London_and_North_Western_Railway" title="London and North Western Railway">London and North Western Railway</a> (L&amp;NWR) into the <a href="/wiki/London,_Midland_and_Scottish_Railway" title="London, Midland and Scottish Railway">London, Midland and Scottish Railway</a> (LMS), and the LMS adopted the LNWR's (the "Premier Line") <a href="/wiki/Euston_railway_station" title="Euston railway station">Euston station</a> as its principal London terminus. The Midland Grand Hotel was closed in 1935, and the building was subsequently used as offices for <a href="/wiki/British_Railways" class="mw-redirect" title="British Railways">British Railways</a>. During <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, bombing inflicted damage on the train shed, which was only partially reglazed after the war.<sup id="cite_ref-bbchow_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbchow-35">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> On the night of 10–11 May 1941 a bomb fell onto the station floor at platform 3, exploding in the beer vaults underneath. The station was not significantly damaged, but was closed for eight days, with platforms 2–3 remaining closed until June. In 1947 the St. Pancras junction was relaid with prefabricated trackwork, along with associated changes to the signalling system.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJackson198472_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJackson198472-34">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On the creation of <a href="/wiki/British_Rail" title="British Rail">British Railways</a> (BR) in 1948, St Pancras received a significant investment after neglect by the LMS.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJackson198472_34-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJackson198472-34">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Destinations included the London area services to North Woolwich, St Albans and Bedford. Long-distance trains reached Glasgow, Leeds, Nottingham, Sheffield and Manchester, with famous named trains including <i><a href="/wiki/The_Palatine" title="The Palatine">The Palatine</a></i> to Manchester,<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> <i>The <a href="/wiki/Thames-Clyde_Express" class="mw-redirect" title="Thames-Clyde Express">Thames-Clyde Express</a></i> to Glasgow,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHolland2012102_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHolland2012102-37">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> and <i>The <a href="/wiki/Master_Cutler_(train)" title="Master Cutler (train)">Master Cutler</a></i> to Sheffield (transferred from King's Cross in 1966, which itself had transferred from <a href="/wiki/Marylebone_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Marylebone railway station">Marylebone</a> eight years earlier).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJones2017195_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJones2017195-38">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 7 October 1957, the signalling at St Pancras was upgraded, replacing the three original boxes with a power box controlling 205 route switches and 33 points over a network of 1,400 relays.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJackson198474_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJackson198474-39">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> From 1960 to 1966, electrification work on the <a href="/wiki/West_Coast_Main_Line" title="West Coast Main Line">West Coast Main Line</a> between London and Manchester saw a new <a href="/wiki/Midland_Pullman" title="Midland Pullman">Midland Pullman</a> from Manchester to St Pancras.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPalmer2017211–212_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPalmer2017211–212-40">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> These trains and those to Glasgow were withdrawn following the completion of the rebuilding of Euston and the consolidation of these services.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHolland2012102_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHolland2012102-37">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:St_Pancras_2_railway_station_2115487_10c7b92d.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/St_Pancras_2_railway_station_2115487_10c7b92d.jpg/220px-St_Pancras_2_railway_station_2115487_10c7b92d.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="133" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/St_Pancras_2_railway_station_2115487_10c7b92d.jpg/330px-St_Pancras_2_railway_station_2115487_10c7b92d.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/St_Pancras_2_railway_station_2115487_10c7b92d.jpg/440px-St_Pancras_2_railway_station_2115487_10c7b92d.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="619" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:St_Pancras_2_railway_station_2115487_10c7b92d.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An express to Leicester awaiting departure in 1957</div></div></div>
<p>By the 1960s, St Pancras was seen as redundant, and several attempts were made to close it and demolish the hotel (by then known as St Pancras Chambers). These attempts provoked strong and successful opposition, with the campaign led by the later <a href="/wiki/Poet_Laureate" class="mw-redirect" title="Poet Laureate">Poet Laureate</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Betjeman" title="John Betjeman">John Betjeman</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cnjjb_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnjjb-41">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-dtsg_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dtsg-42">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jane_Hughes_Fawcett" class="mw-redirect" title="Jane Hughes Fawcett">Jane Hughes Fawcett</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Victorian_Society" class="mw-redirect" title="Victorian Society">Victorian Society</a> was instrumental in its preservation, and was dubbed "the furious Mrs. Fawcett" by British rail officials.<sup id="cite_ref-washpostobit_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-washpostobit-43">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> Many of the demonstrators had witnessed the demolition of the nearby <a href="/wiki/Euston_Arch" title="Euston Arch">Euston Arch</a> a few years previously, and were strongly opposed to the distinctive architecture of St Pancras suffering the same fate.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJackson198473_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJackson198473-44">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> The station became Grade I listed building in November 1967, preventing any drastic modifications.<sup id="cite_ref-NHLE_8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NHLE-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> The plans were scrapped by BR in December 1968, realising that it was more cost-effective to modernise the hotel instead, though they disliked owning it.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJackson198473_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJackson198473-44">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Resting_Between_Duties.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Resting_Between_Duties.jpg/220px-Resting_Between_Duties.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Resting_Between_Duties.jpg/330px-Resting_Between_Duties.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Resting_Between_Duties.jpg/440px-Resting_Between_Duties.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="422" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Resting_Between_Duties.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>St Pancras, semi-derelict in 1984</div></div></div>
<p>In the 1970s, the train shed roof was in danger of collapse, and the newly appointed Director of Environment <a href="/wiki/Bernard_Kaukas" title="Bernard Kaukas">Bernard Kaukas</a> persuaded the company to invest £3m to save it.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> In 1978, a <i><a href="/wiki/Private_Eye" title="Private Eye">Private Eye</a></i> piece said that British Rail really wanted to demolish St Pancras but were opposed by "a lot of long-haired sentimentalists" and "faceless bureaucrats" and praised the office blocks that replaced the Euston Arch.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBradley201011_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBradley201011-46">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After the <a href="/wiki/History_of_rail_transport_in_Great_Britain_1948-1994#The_1980s_:_Sectorisation" class="mw-redirect" title="History of rail transport in Great Britain 1948-1994">sectorisation of British Rail</a> in 1986, main-line services to the East Midlands were provided by the <a href="/wiki/InterCity_(British_Rail)" title="InterCity (British Rail)">InterCity</a> sector, with suburban services to St Albans, Luton and Bedford by <a href="/wiki/Network_SouthEast" title="Network SouthEast">Network SouthEast</a>. In 1988 the <a href="/wiki/Snow_Hill_Tunnel_(London)" class="mw-redirect" title="Snow Hill Tunnel (London)">Snow Hill tunnel</a> re-opened resulting in the creation of the Thameslink route and the resultant diversion of the majority of suburban trains to the new route. The station continued to be served by trains running on the Midland main line to Leicester, Nottingham and Sheffield, together with a few suburban services to Bedford and Luton.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBradley2010161_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBradley2010161-47">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> These constituted only a few trains an hour and left the station underused.<sup id="cite_ref-bbchow_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbchow-35">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Following the <a href="/wiki/Privatisation_of_British_Rail" title="Privatisation of British Rail">privatisation of British Rail</a>, the long-distance services from St Pancras were franchised to <a href="/wiki/Midland_Mainline" title="Midland Mainline">Midland Mainline</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Train_operating_company" title="Train operating company">train operating company</a> owned by <a href="/wiki/National_Express" title="National Express">National Express</a>, starting on 28 April 1996. The few remaining suburban trains still operating into St Pancras were operated by the <a href="/wiki/Thameslink_(train_operating_company_1997-2006)" class="mw-redirect" title="Thameslink (train operating company 1997-2006)">Thameslink</a> train operating company, owned by <a href="/wiki/Govia" title="Govia">Govia</a>, from 2 March 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-ironroad_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ironroad-48">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A small number of trains to and from Leeds were introduced, mainly because the High Speed Train sets were maintained there and were already running empty north of Sheffield. During the 2000s major rebuild of the West Coast Main Line, St Pancras again temporarily hosted direct and regular inter-city trains to Manchester, this time via the <a href="/wiki/Hope_Valley_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="Hope Valley Line">Hope Valley route</a> (via the Dore South curve) under the title of <i>Project Rio</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-regrio_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-regrio-49">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="New_role">New role</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St_Pancras_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: New role">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:KingsCrossDevelopmentModel.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/KingsCrossDevelopmentModel.jpg/220px-KingsCrossDevelopmentModel.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/KingsCrossDevelopmentModel.jpg/330px-KingsCrossDevelopmentModel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/KingsCrossDevelopmentModel.jpg/440px-KingsCrossDevelopmentModel.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:KingsCrossDevelopmentModel.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Model of the extended St Pancras station (left) and King's Cross station (right, seen before restoration circa 2012)</div></div></div>
<p>The original plan for the Channel Tunnel Rail Link (CTRL) involved a tunnel from south-east of London to an underground terminus in the vicinity of King's Cross. However, a late change of plan, principally driven by the then <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_the_Environment" title="Secretary of State for the Environment">Secretary of State for the Environment</a> <a href="/wiki/Michael_Heseltine" title="Michael Heseltine">Michael Heseltine</a>'s desire for <a href="/wiki/Urban_regeneration" class="mw-redirect" title="Urban regeneration">urban regeneration</a> in east London, led to a change of route, with the new line approaching London from the east. This opened the possibility of reusing St Pancras as the terminus, with access via the <a href="/wiki/North_London_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="North London Line">North London Line</a>, which crosses the throat of the station.<sup id="cite_ref-bbchow_35-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbchow-35">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mrfcr_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mrfcr-50">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The idea of using the North London line was rejected in 1994 by the <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_Transport" title="Secretary of State for Transport">transport secretary</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_MacGregor,_Baron_MacGregor_of_Pulham_Market" title="John MacGregor, Baron MacGregor of Pulham Market">John MacGregor</a>, as "difficult to construct and environmentally damaging". However, the idea of using St Pancras station as the terminus was retained, albeit now linked by 12.4 miles (20&#160;km) of new tunnels to <a href="/wiki/Dagenham" title="Dagenham">Dagenham</a> via <a href="/wiki/Stratford,_London" title="Stratford, London">Stratford</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bbchow_35-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbchow-35">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mrfcr_50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mrfcr-50">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/London_and_Continental_Railways" title="London and Continental Railways">London and Continental Railways</a> (LCR), created at the time of British Rail privatisation, was selected by the government in 1996 to reconstruct St Pancras, build the CTRL, and take over the British share of the Eurostar operation.  LCR had owned St Pancras station since privatisation to allow the station to be redeveloped. Financial difficulties in 1998, and the collapse of <a href="/wiki/Railtrack" title="Railtrack">Railtrack</a> in 2001, caused some revision of this plan, but LCR retained ownership of the station.<sup id="cite_ref-LCR_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LCR-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The design and project management of reconstruction was undertaken on behalf of LCR by Rail Link Engineering (RLE), a consortium of <a href="/wiki/Bechtel" title="Bechtel">Bechtel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arup_Group_Limited" class="mw-redirect" title="Arup Group Limited">Arup</a>, <a href="/wiki/Systra" class="mw-redirect" title="Systra">Systra</a> and <a href="/wiki/Halcrow_Group_Limited" class="mw-redirect" title="Halcrow Group Limited">Halcrow</a>. The original reference design for the station was by <a href="/wiki/Nick_Derbyshire_(architect)" title="Nick Derbyshire (architect)">Nick Derbyshire</a>, former head of British Rail's in-house architecture team. The master plan of the complex was by <a href="/wiki/Foster_and_Partners" title="Foster and Partners">Foster and Partners</a>, and the lead architect of the reconstruction was <a href="/wiki/Alastair_Lansley" title="Alastair Lansley">Alistair Lansley</a>, a former colleague of Nick Derbyshire recruited by RLE.<sup id="cite_ref-mrspi_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mrspi-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mrlcr_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mrlcr-51">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bloom_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bloom-52">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>To accommodate 300-metre+ <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_373" title="British Rail Class 373">Eurostar trains</a>, and to provide capacity for the existing trains to the Midlands and the new Kent services on the high-speed rail link, the train shed was extended a considerable distance northwards by a new flat-roofed shed. The station was initially planned to have 13 platforms under this extended train shed. <a href="/wiki/East_Midlands" title="East Midlands">East Midlands</a> services would use the western platforms, Eurostar services the middle platforms, and Kent services the eastern platforms. The Eurostar platforms and one of the Midland platforms would extend back into the Barlow train shed. Access to Eurostar for departing passengers would be via a departure suite on the west of the station, and then to the platforms by a bridge above the tracks within the historic train shed. Arriving Eurostar passengers would leave the station by a new concourse at its north end.<sup id="cite_ref-mrfcr_50-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mrfcr-50">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>This original design was later modified, with access to the Eurostar platforms from below, using the station undercroft and allowing the deletion of the visually intrusive bridge. By dropping the extension of any of the Midland platforms into the train shed, space was freed up to allow wells to be constructed in the station floor, which provided daylight and access to the undercroft.<sup id="cite_ref-mrfcr_50-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mrfcr-50">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The reconstruction of the station was recorded in the <a href="/wiki/BBC_Television" title="BBC Television">BBC Television</a> documentary series <i>The Eight Hundred Million Pound Railway Station</i> broadcast as six 30-minute episodes between 13‒28 November 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rebuilding">Rebuilding</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St_Pancras_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Rebuilding">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:StPOlympics.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/StPOlympics.jpg/220px-StPOlympics.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/StPOlympics.jpg/330px-StPOlympics.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/StPOlympics.jpg/440px-StPOlympics.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="2000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:StPOlympics.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>The Meeting Place</i> and the Olympic Rings for the <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics" title="2012 Summer Olympics">2012 Summer Olympics</a></div></div></div>
<p>By early 2004, the eastern side of the extended train shed was complete, and the Barlow train shed was closed to trains.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> From 12 April 2004, Midland Mainline trains terminated at an interim station occupying the eastern part of the extension immediately adjacent to the entrance.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As part of the construction of the western side of the new train shed that now began, an underground "box" was constructed to house new platforms for Thameslink, which at this point ran partially under the extended station. In order for this to happen, the existing Thameslink tunnels between <a href="/wiki/Kentish_Town_station" title="Kentish Town station">Kentish Town</a> and <a href="/wiki/King%27s_Cross_Thameslink_railway_station" title="King&#39;s Cross Thameslink railway station">King's Cross Thameslink</a> were closed between 11 September 2004 and 15 May 2005 while the works were carried out. Thameslink services from the north terminated in the same platforms as the Midland Main Line trains, while services from the south terminated at King's Cross Thameslink.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-56">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>When the lines were re-opened, the new <a href="/wiki/Station_box" title="Station box">station box</a> was still only a bare concrete shell and could not take passengers. Thameslink trains reverted to their previous route but ran through the station box without stopping. The budget for the Channel Tunnel Rail Link works did not include work on the fitting out of the station, as these works had originally been part of the separate <a href="/wiki/Thameslink_Programme" title="Thameslink Programme">Thameslink 2000</a> works programme.  Despite lobbying by rail operators who wished to see the station open at the same time as St Pancras International, the Government failed to provide additional funding to allow the fit out works to be completed immediately following the line blockade. Eventually, on 8 February 2006, <a href="/wiki/Alistair_Darling" title="Alistair Darling">Alistair Darling</a>, the Secretary of State for Transport, announced £50&#160;million funding for the fit-out of the station, plus another £10–15&#160;million for the installation of associated <a href="/wiki/Railway_signalling" title="Railway signalling">signalling</a> and other lineside works.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-56">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bbcghost_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbcghost-57">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bbcgoatl_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbcgoatl-58">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Midland_Grand_Hotel_extension_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Midland_Grand_Hotel_extension_1.jpg/220px-Midland_Grand_Hotel_extension_1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Midland_Grand_Hotel_extension_1.jpg/330px-Midland_Grand_Hotel_extension_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Midland_Grand_Hotel_extension_1.jpg/440px-Midland_Grand_Hotel_extension_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Midland_Grand_Hotel_extension_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>St Pancras Renaissance London Hotel extension under construction</div></div></div>
<p>The fit-out works were designed by <a href="/wiki/Chapman_Taylor" title="Chapman Taylor">Chapman Taylor</a><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> and Arup (Eurostar) and completed by ISG Interior Plc Contractors<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> collaborating with Bechtel as Project Managers.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> The client was London and Continental Railways who were advised by <a href="/wiki/Hitachi_Consulting" title="Hitachi Consulting">Hitachi Consulting</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2005, planning consent was granted for a refurbishment of the former Midland Grand Hotel building, with plans to refurbish and extend it as a hotel and apartment block.<sup id="cite_ref-sleeper_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sleeper-63">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> The newly refurbished hotel opened to guests on 21 March 2011 with a grand opening ceremony on 5 May.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>By the middle of 2006, the western side of the train shed extension was completed.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> The rebuilding cost was in the region of £800&#160;million,<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> up from an initial estimate of £310&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_station">International station</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St_Pancras_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: International station">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In early November 2007, Eurostar conducted a testing programme in which some 6000 members of the public were involved in passenger check-in, immigration control and departure trials, during which the "passengers" each made three return journeys out of St Pancras to the entrance to the London tunnel. On 4 September 2007, the first test train ran from <a href="/wiki/Gare_du_Nord" title="Gare du Nord">Paris Gare du Nord</a> to St Pancras.<sup id="cite_ref-bbcfout_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbcfout-68">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> Children's illustrator <a href="/wiki/Quentin_Blake" title="Quentin Blake">Quentin Blake</a> was commissioned to provide a huge mural of an "imaginary welcoming committee" as a disguise for one of the remaining ramshackle Stanley Building South immediately opposite the station exit.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>St Pancras was officially re-opened as St Pancras International, and the High Speed 1 service was launched on 6 November 2007 by <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Queen Elizabeth II</a> and <a href="/wiki/Prince_Philip,_Duke_of_Edinburgh" title="Prince Philip, Duke of Edinburgh">the Duke of Edinburgh</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-mropc_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mropc-70">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-stpqe_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stpqe-71">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> Services were extended to <a href="/wiki/Rotterdam" title="Rotterdam">Rotterdam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a> in April 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-eurostarholland_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eurostarholland-73">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During an elaborate opening ceremony, actor <a href="/wiki/Timothy_West" title="Timothy West">Timothy West</a>, as Henry Barlow, addressed the audience, which was also entertained by the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Philharmonic_Orchestra" title="Royal Philharmonic Orchestra">Royal Philharmonic Orchestra</a> and the singers <a href="/wiki/Lemar" title="Lemar">Lemar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Katherine_Jenkins" title="Katherine Jenkins">Katherine Jenkins</a>. In a carefully staged set piece, the first <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_395" title="British Rail Class 395">Class 395</a> train and two <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_373" title="British Rail Class 373">Class 373</a> trains arrived through a cloud of <a href="/wiki/Dry_ice" title="Dry ice">dry ice</a> in adjacent platforms within seconds of each other.<sup id="cite_ref-mropc_70-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mropc-70">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-stpqe_71-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stpqe-71">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> During the ceremony, Paul Day's large bronze statue <i>The Meeting Place</i> was also unveiled. At a much smaller ceremony on 12 November 2007, the bronze statue of John Betjeman by sculptor <a href="/wiki/Martin_Jennings" title="Martin Jennings">Martin Jennings</a> was unveiled by Betjeman's daughter, the author <a href="/wiki/Candida_Lycett_Green" title="Candida Lycett Green">Candida Lycett Green</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-betjeman-unveiled_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-betjeman-unveiled-74">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> Public service by Eurostar train via High Speed 1 started on 14 November 2007. In a small ceremony, station staff cut a ribbon leading to the Eurostar platforms.<sup id="cite_ref-gronop_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gronop-75">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> In the same month, services to the East Midlands were transferred to a new franchisee, <a href="/wiki/East_Midlands_Trains" title="East Midlands Trains">East Midlands Trains</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> The low-level Thameslink platforms opened on 9 December 2007, replacing King's Cross Thameslink.<sup id="cite_ref-bbctlop_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbctlop-77">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>St Pancras has retained a reputation of having one of the most recognisable facades of all the London termini, and known as the "cathedral of the railways".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMason20167_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMason20167-30">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> In <i>Britain's 100 Best Railway Stations</i> by <a href="/wiki/Simon_Jenkins" title="Simon Jenkins">Simon Jenkins</a>, the station was one of only ten to be awarded five stars.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> The station has <a href="/wiki/Bilingual" class="mw-redirect" title="Bilingual">bilingual</a> signs in <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a> and <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a>, one of the few in England to do so.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Services">Services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St_Pancras_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:St_Pancras_international_entrance.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/St_Pancras_international_entrance.jpg/220px-St_Pancras_international_entrance.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/St_Pancras_international_entrance.jpg/330px-St_Pancras_international_entrance.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/St_Pancras_international_entrance.jpg/440px-St_Pancras_international_entrance.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3888" data-file-height="2592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:St_Pancras_international_entrance.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>East side entrance from Pancras Road</div></div></div>
<p>St Pancras contains four groups of platforms on two levels, accessed via the main concourse at ground level.  The below-surface group contains through <a href="/wiki/Railway_platform" title="Railway platform">platforms</a> A and B, and the upper level has three groups of terminal platforms: domestic platforms 1–4 and 11–13 on each side of international platforms 5–10.  Platforms A &amp; B serve Thameslink, 1–4 connect to the <a href="/wiki/Midland_Main_Line" title="Midland Main Line">Midland Main Line</a>, while platforms 11–13 lead to <a href="/wiki/High_Speed_1" title="High Speed 1">High Speed 1</a>; there is no connection between the two lines, except for a maintenance siding outside the station.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> There are also a variety of shops and restaurants within the station concourse.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The station is the London terminus for Eurostar's high-speed trains to Paris, Brussels, <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lille" title="Lille">Lille</a> via the Channel Tunnel.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-eurostarholland_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eurostarholland-73">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> It is also the terminus for <a href="/wiki/East_Midlands_Railway" title="East Midlands Railway">East Midlands Railway</a> services from London to <a href="/wiki/Derby_railway_station" title="Derby railway station">Derby</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leicester_railway_station" title="Leicester railway station">Leicester</a>, Nottingham, Sheffield, and smaller towns en route. <a href="/wiki/Thameslink_and_Great_Northern" class="mw-redirect" title="Thameslink and Great Northern">Thameslink</a> trains on the cross-London Thameslink route call at platforms beneath the main station, south to <a href="/wiki/Gatwick_Airport_railway_station" title="Gatwick Airport railway station">Gatwick Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brighton_railway_station" title="Brighton railway station">Brighton</a> and north to Luton Airport Parkway for <a href="/wiki/Luton_Airport" title="Luton Airport">Luton Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bedford_railway_station" title="Bedford railway station">Bedford</a>. High-speed domestic services to Kent, run by Southeastern, depart on the same level as Eurostar &amp; East Midlands Railway.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:On_arrival_130723_2.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/On_arrival_130723_2.JPG/220px-On_arrival_130723_2.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/On_arrival_130723_2.JPG/330px-On_arrival_130723_2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/On_arrival_130723_2.JPG/440px-On_arrival_130723_2.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:On_arrival_130723_2.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Arriving on one of the Eurostar platforms</div></div></div>
<p>The terminal is one of relatively few railway stations in England to feature multilingual signage in English and French.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> In March 2014, the station's public relations team commissioned a study of mispronounced words, reportedly as a result of passengers referring to the station as "St <a href="/wiki/Pancreas" title="Pancreas">Pancreas</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Platform_layout">Platform layout</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St_Pancras_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Platform layout">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:StPancrasInternational-PS02.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/StPancrasInternational-PS02.JPG/220px-StPancrasInternational-PS02.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/StPancrasInternational-PS02.JPG/330px-StPancrasInternational-PS02.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/StPancrasInternational-PS02.JPG/440px-StPancrasInternational-PS02.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:StPancrasInternational-PS02.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Interior of station, with <a href="/wiki/Eurostar" title="Eurostar">Eurostar</a> train awaiting departure at left</div></div></div>
<p>The longer international platforms, used by Eurostar, extend into Barlow's train shed, whilst the other platforms terminate at the southern end of the 2005 extension. The international platforms do not occupy the full width of the Barlow train shed, and sections of the floor area have been opened up to provide natural light to the new ground-level concourse below.  Eurostar's arrival and departure lounges lie below these platforms, adjacent to <i>The Arcade</i>, a concourse fashioned from the original station undercroft which runs along the western length of the Barlow train shed.  The southern end of <i>The Arcade</i> links to the western ticket hall of King's Cross St Pancras tube station.<sup id="cite_ref-mrspi_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mrspi-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-spsplp_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spsplp-87">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-spsslp_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spsslp-88">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Access to the East Midlands Railway platforms are via the northern end of <i>The Arcade</i>, while the Thameslink and domestic High Speed platforms are reached via a street-level concourse where the old and new parts of the station meet. The main pedestrian entrance is at the eastern end of this concourse, where a subway enables pedestrians to reach King's Cross station and the northern ticket hall of the tube station.<sup id="cite_ref-mrspi_11-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mrspi-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-89">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Domestic_services">Domestic services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St_Pancras_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Domestic services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="East_Midlands_Railway">East Midlands Railway</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St_Pancras_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: East Midlands Railway">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:St_Pancras_railway_station_MMB_A5_222012_222003_43055_373XXX.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/St_Pancras_railway_station_MMB_A5_222012_222003_43055_373XXX.jpg/220px-St_Pancras_railway_station_MMB_A5_222012_222003_43055_373XXX.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/St_Pancras_railway_station_MMB_A5_222012_222003_43055_373XXX.jpg/330px-St_Pancras_railway_station_MMB_A5_222012_222003_43055_373XXX.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/St_Pancras_railway_station_MMB_A5_222012_222003_43055_373XXX.jpg/440px-St_Pancras_railway_station_MMB_A5_222012_222003_43055_373XXX.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3760" data-file-height="2440" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:St_Pancras_railway_station_MMB_A5_222012_222003_43055_373XXX.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Two Class 222 <i>Meridian</i> diesel multiple units and a Class 43 HST diesel set operated by <a href="/wiki/East_Midlands_Railway" title="East Midlands Railway">East Midlands Railway</a>, at the <a href="/wiki/Midland_Main_Line" title="Midland Main Line">Midland Main Line</a> platforms</div></div></div>
<p>Since 2019, platforms 1–4 have been the southern terminus for Midland Main Line trains operated by East Midlands Railway to/from the East Midlands and Yorkshire, including Leicester, Corby, Nottingham, <a href="/wiki/Kettering_railway_station" title="Kettering railway station">Kettering</a>, Derby and Sheffield. Occasional trains also run to <a href="/wiki/Melton_Mowbray_railway_station" title="Melton Mowbray railway station">Melton Mowbray</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lincoln_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Lincoln railway station">Lincoln</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leeds_railway_station" title="Leeds railway station">Leeds</a>, <a href="/wiki/York_railway_station" title="York railway station">York</a> and <a href="/wiki/Scarborough_railway_station" title="Scarborough railway station">Scarborough</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-EMT_Timetable_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EMT_Timetable-90">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As of September 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=St_Pancras_railway_station&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, the Monday-Saturday off-peak timetable has five services per hour: three fast and two semi-fast.<sup id="cite_ref-EMT_Timetable_90-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EMT_Timetable-90">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Thameslink">Thameslink</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St_Pancras_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Thameslink">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stpancrasthameslink.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/1d/Stpancrasthameslink.jpg/220px-Stpancrasthameslink.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/1d/Stpancrasthameslink.jpg/330px-Stpancrasthameslink.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/1d/Stpancrasthameslink.jpg/440px-Stpancrasthameslink.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1728" data-file-height="1152" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stpancrasthameslink.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Thameslink platforms at St Pancras (2007)</div></div></div>
<p>As part of the Thameslink Programme, St Pancras International gained platforms on the Thameslink route, replacing King's Cross Thameslink to the south-east. In line with the former station, the Thameslink platforms are designated A and B.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> The new platforms have met with some criticism for the length of the walking route to the underground as compared with King's Cross Thameslink.
The Thameslink Programme involves the introduction of 12-car trains across the enlarged Thameslink network.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> As extending the platforms at King's Cross Thameslink was thought to be impractical (requiring alterations to Clerkenwell No 3 tunnel and the <a href="/wiki/Circle_line_(London_Underground)" title="Circle line (London Underground)">Circle</a>/<a href="/wiki/Hammersmith_%26_City_line" title="Hammersmith &amp; City line">Hammersmith &amp; City</a>/<a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_line" title="Metropolitan line">Metropolitan</a> <a href="/wiki/London_Underground" title="London Underground">Underground</a> lines, which would be extremely disruptive and prohibitively expensive), it was decided to build new Thameslink platforms under St Pancras.<sup id="cite_ref-kxc_description_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kxc_description-94">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Thameslink platforms serve trains to <a href="/wiki/Bedford_railway_station" title="Bedford railway station">Bedford</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luton_railway_station" title="Luton railway station">Luton</a>, <a href="/wiki/St_Albans_City_railway_station" title="St Albans City railway station">St Albans City</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_railway_station" title="Cambridge railway station">Cambridge</a> and <a href="/wiki/Peterborough_railway_station" title="Peterborough railway station">Peterborough</a> in the north, and <a href="/wiki/Wimbledon_station" title="Wimbledon station">Wimbledon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sutton_railway_station_(London)" title="Sutton railway station (London)">Sutton</a>, <a href="/wiki/East_Croydon_station" title="East Croydon station">East Croydon</a>, Gatwick Airport and Brighton in the south.<sup id="cite_ref-Railplan2020_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Railplan2020-95">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Southeastern">Southeastern</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St_Pancras_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Southeastern">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:St_Pancras_railway_station_MMB_E1_395025.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/St_Pancras_railway_station_MMB_E1_395025.jpg/220px-St_Pancras_railway_station_MMB_E1_395025.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/St_Pancras_railway_station_MMB_E1_395025.jpg/330px-St_Pancras_railway_station_MMB_E1_395025.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/St_Pancras_railway_station_MMB_E1_395025.jpg/440px-St_Pancras_railway_station_MMB_E1_395025.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3708" data-file-height="2424" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:St_Pancras_railway_station_MMB_E1_395025.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The high speed domestic platforms with <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_395" title="British Rail Class 395">Class 395 "Javelin"</a> units</div></div></div>
<p>Southeastern runs high-speed Class 395 trains on High Speed 1 to Kent and the South East, to <a href="/wiki/Faversham" title="Faversham">Faversham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Margate_railway_station" title="Margate railway station">Margate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ramsgate_railway_station" title="Ramsgate railway station">Ramsgate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canterbury_West_railway_station" title="Canterbury West railway station">Canterbury West</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dover_Priory_railway_station" title="Dover Priory railway station">Dover Priory</a>, <a href="/wiki/Folkestone_Central_railway_station" title="Folkestone Central railway station">Folkestone Central</a>, Ashford, Ebbsfleet International and other destinations in Kent.
</p><p>The first domestic service carrying passengers over High Speed 1 ran on 12 December 2008, to mark one year before regular services were due to begin. This special service, carrying various dignitaries, ran from Ashford International to St Pancras.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> Starting in June 2009, Southeastern provided a preview service between St Pancras and Ebbsfleet, extending to Ashford International during peak hours.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> In September, Southeastern extended the peak-time services to Dover and Ramsgate.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> The full service began on 13 December.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>Departures</b>
</p>
