<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Olympic_Javelin_service">Olympic Javelin service</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St_Pancras_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Olympic Javelin service">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics" title="2012 Summer Olympics">2012 Summer Olympics</a> in London, St Pancras was the Central London terminus of the <i><a href="/wiki/Olympic_Javelin" class="mw-redirect" title="Olympic Javelin">Olympic Javelin</a></i> service, a seven-minute shuttle between Central London and <a href="/wiki/Stratford_International_station" title="Stratford International station">Stratford International station</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Park,_London" class="mw-redirect" title="Olympic Park, London">London Olympic Park</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-oljav_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oljav-100">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_services">International services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St_Pancras_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: International services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eurostar_trains_at_St_Pancras.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Eurostar_trains_at_St_Pancras.jpg/220px-Eurostar_trains_at_St_Pancras.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Eurostar_trains_at_St_Pancras.jpg/330px-Eurostar_trains_at_St_Pancras.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Eurostar_trains_at_St_Pancras.jpg/440px-Eurostar_trains_at_St_Pancras.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eurostar_trains_at_St_Pancras.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Eurostar train at St Pancras International</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Eurostar" title="Eurostar">Eurostar</a></div>
<p>Seventeen pairs of Eurostar trains to and from Paris Gare du Nord every day, ten pairs of trains to and from <a href="/wiki/Brussels-South_railway_station" title="Brussels-South railway station">Bruxelles-Midi/Brussel-Zuid</a> for <a href="/wiki/Brussels_and_the_European_Union" title="Brussels and the European Union">Brussels and the European Union</a> de facto capital, and one train to and from <a href="/wiki/Gare_de_Marne-la-Vall%C3%A9e_-_Chessy" class="mw-redirect" title="Gare de Marne-la-Vallée - Chessy">Marne-la-Vallée</a> for <a href="/wiki/Disneyland_Resort_Paris" class="mw-redirect" title="Disneyland Resort Paris">Disneyland Resort Paris</a>. Extra services run to Paris on Fridays and Sundays, with a reduced service to Brussels at weekends. Additional weekend leisure-oriented trains run to the <a href="/wiki/French_Alps" title="French Alps">French Alps</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Skiing" title="Skiing">skiing</a> season, and to <a href="/wiki/Marseille" title="Marseille">Marseille</a> via <a href="/wiki/Lyon" title="Lyon">Lyon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Avignon" title="Avignon">Avignon</a> in the summer.<sup id="cite_ref-mrnes_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mrnes-101">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-eurott_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eurott-102">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> It also serves as the terminus for services to <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a> from Spring 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> Trains call at a mix of four intermediate stations (Ebbsfleet International, Ashford International, <a href="/wiki/Gare_de_Calais-Fr%C3%A9thun" title="Gare de Calais-Fréthun">Calais-Fréthun</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gare_de_Lille_Europe" title="Gare de Lille Europe">Lille-Europe</a>), with some running non-stop. Non-stop trains take 2 hours 15 minutes to Paris, and just under 1 hour 50 minutes to Brussels, other trains taking 5 or 10 minutes longer depending on whether they make one or two stops.<sup id="cite_ref-mrnes_101-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mrnes-101">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-eurott_102-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eurott-102">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>St Pancras International is one of four railway stations in the UK with <a href="/wiki/Juxtaposed_controls" title="Juxtaposed controls">juxtaposed</a> immigration control facilities set up by the <a href="/wiki/French_Border_Police" class="mw-redirect" title="French Border Police">French Border Police</a> to clear passengers for entry into France and the rest of the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen Area</a> prior to boarding the trains.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> Passengers do not need any further immigration or passport checks after entering the main departure gates, or at the corresponding gate at the other end on return journeys, as they are cleared by the <a href="/wiki/UK_Border_Force" class="mw-redirect" title="UK Border Force">UK Border Force</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Creative_arts">Creative arts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St_Pancras_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Creative arts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Meeting_Place_-_St_Pancras.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c6/The_Meeting_Place_-_St_Pancras.jpg/170px-The_Meeting_Place_-_St_Pancras.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c6/The_Meeting_Place_-_St_Pancras.jpg/255px-The_Meeting_Place_-_St_Pancras.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c6/The_Meeting_Place_-_St_Pancras.jpg/340px-The_Meeting_Place_-_St_Pancras.jpg 2x" data-file-width="720" data-file-height="960" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Meeting_Place_-_St_Pancras.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/The_Meeting_Place_(sculpture)" title="The Meeting Place (sculpture)">The Meeting Place</a></i> sculpture at St Pancras</div></div></div>
<p>There are several works of art on public display at St Pancras. A 9-metre (29.5&#160;ft) high 20-tonne (19.7-long-ton; 22.0-short-ton) bronze statue titled <i><a href="/wiki/The_Meeting_Place_(sculpture)" title="The Meeting Place (sculpture)">The Meeting Place</a></i> stands at the south end of the upper level beneath the station clock. It was designed by the British artist <a href="/wiki/Paul_Day_(sculptor)" title="Paul Day (sculptor)">Paul Day</a> to evoke the romance of travel through the depiction of a couple locked in an amorous embrace.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc-meetingplace_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-meetingplace-106">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> Controversy was caused by Day's 2008 addition of a bronze relief <a href="/wiki/Frieze" title="Frieze">frieze</a> around the plinth,<sup id="cite_ref-times-meetingplace_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-times-meetingplace-107">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> depicting a commuter falling into the path of an <a href="/wiki/London_Underground_rolling_stock" title="London Underground rolling stock">Underground train</a> driven by the <a href="/wiki/Grim_Reaper" class="mw-redirect" title="Grim Reaper">Grim Reaper</a>. Day revised the frieze before the final version was installed.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Alberto_giurioli.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Alberto_giurioli.jpg/220px-Alberto_giurioli.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Alberto_giurioli.jpg/330px-Alberto_giurioli.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Alberto_giurioli.jpg/440px-Alberto_giurioli.jpg 2x" data-file-width="960" data-file-height="640" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Alberto_giurioli.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>One of the pianos in the St Pancras concourse</div></div></div>
<p>On the upper level, above the Arcade concourse, stands a bronze <a href="/wiki/Statue_of_John_Betjeman" title="Statue of John Betjeman">statue of John Betjeman</a>, depicted gazing in apparent wonder at the Barlow roof. A work of the British sculptor <a href="/wiki/Martin_Jennings" title="Martin Jennings">Martin Jennings</a>, the statue commemorates Betjeman's successful campaign to save the station from demolition in the 1960s.<sup id="cite_ref-cnjjb_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnjjb-41">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> The 2-metre (6&#160;ft 7&#160;in)-high statue stands on a flat disc of Cumbrian <a href="/wiki/Slate" title="Slate">slate</a> inscribed with lines from Betjeman's poem <i>Cornish Cliffs</i>:
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886047036">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>And in the shadowless unclouded glare / Deep blue above us fades to whiteness where / A misty sea-line meets the wash of air.</p><div class="templatequotecite">—&#8201;<cite>John Betjeman, Cornish Cliffs, <sup id="cite_ref-jennings-betjeman_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jennings-betjeman-110">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup></cite></div>
</blockquote>
<p>There are a number of <a href="/wiki/Upright_piano" class="mw-redirect" title="Upright piano">upright pianos</a> in the main St Pancras concourse that are available for anyone to play. In 2016, <a href="/wiki/Elton_John" title="Elton John">Elton John</a> gave an impromptu performance here on a piano he subsequently donated to the station as a gift.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> In 2017, the <a href="/wiki/B_Positive_Choir" title="B Positive Choir">B Positive Choir</a>, formed to raise awareness of <a href="/wiki/Sickle-cell_disease" class="mw-redirect" title="Sickle-cell disease">sickle-cell disease</a>, performed a Christmas concert in the station concourse.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2016, <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a> opened <a href="/wiki/YouTube_Space" class="mw-redirect" title="YouTube Space">YouTube Space</a>, a creative centre for <a href="/wiki/Vlogger" class="mw-redirect" title="Vlogger">vloggers</a> inside the company's new 20,000-square-foot (1,900&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) premises on Pancras Square adjacent to the station. The premises includes a 150-seat cinema and various stages.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Hotel">Hotel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St_Pancras_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Hotel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gilbert_Scott%27s_staircase_inside_the_St._Pancras_Hotel.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Gilbert_Scott%27s_staircase_inside_the_St._Pancras_Hotel.jpg/220px-Gilbert_Scott%27s_staircase_inside_the_St._Pancras_Hotel.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Gilbert_Scott%27s_staircase_inside_the_St._Pancras_Hotel.jpg/330px-Gilbert_Scott%27s_staircase_inside_the_St._Pancras_Hotel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Gilbert_Scott%27s_staircase_inside_the_St._Pancras_Hotel.jpg/440px-Gilbert_Scott%27s_staircase_inside_the_St._Pancras_Hotel.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gilbert_Scott%27s_staircase_inside_the_St._Pancras_Hotel.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Gilbert Scott's staircase inside the St Pancras Renaissance Hotel</div></div></div>
<p>The Midland ran a competition for architects to design a hotel to front the station. <a href="/wiki/George_Gilbert_Scott" title="George Gilbert Scott">George Gilbert Scott</a> was persuaded to enter by his friend, Midland director Joseph Lewis, and completed the winning design at home while attending to his son who had fallen ill. Though plans were complete by the end of the year, financial pressure meant construction had to be delayed. Work eventually started in 1868 and the main section of the Midland Grand Hotel opened on 5 May 1873, with the west wing following three years later.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJackson198466_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJackson198466-31">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> The building is primarily brick, but <a href="/wiki/Polychromatic" class="mw-redirect" title="Polychromatic">polychromatic</a>, in a style derived from the <a href="/wiki/Italian_Gothic_architecture" title="Italian Gothic architecture">Italian gothic</a>, and with numerous other architectural influences.<sup id="cite_ref-thpan_19-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thpan-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;b&#93;</a></sup>  Gilbert Scott reused many of the design details from his earlier work at <a href="/wiki/Kelham_Hall" class="mw-redirect" title="Kelham Hall">Kelham Hall</a> designed in 1857 and completed in 1863, but on a much grander scale for St Pancras.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENoszlopyWaterhouse2005285_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENoszlopyWaterhouse2005285-116">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The hotel closed in 1935 and was turned into St Pancras Chambers, a group of offices, with ownership retained by the LNWR.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBradley2010127_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBradley2010127-117">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> In the late 1980s, British Rail sold off and vacated the premises.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBradley2010102_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBradley2010102-118">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Following the decision to connect St Pancras to the Channel Tunnel Rail Link, plans were made to restore the hotel for its original function. Planning permission was granted in 2005 and funded as part of a £50m Government plan to refurbish the station.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHassanienDale201358–60_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHassanienDale201358–60-119">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/St._Pancras_Renaissance_London_Hotel" title="St. Pancras Renaissance London Hotel">St. Pancras Renaissance London Hotel</a> occupies parts of the original building, including the main public rooms, together with a new bedroom wing on the western side of the Barlow train shed. The upper levels of the original building have been redeveloped as apartments by the Manhattan Loft Corporation.<sup id="cite_ref-sleeper_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sleeper-63">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> These have been sublet via <a href="/wiki/Airbnb" title="Airbnb">Airbnb</a> owing to their desired location.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> The hotel held its grand opening on 5 May 2011, exactly 138&#160;years after its original opening.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHassanienDale201360_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHassanienDale201360-122">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The hotel has been used as setting in several films, including <i><a href="/wiki/Chaplin_(film)" title="Chaplin (film)">Chaplin</a></i> (1992), <i><a href="/wiki/Richard_III_(1995_film)" title="Richard III (1995 film)">Richard III</a></i> (1995) and <i><a href="/wiki/From_Hell_(film)" title="From Hell (film)">From Hell</a></i> (2001). It was used for the filming of the <a href="/wiki/Spice_Girls" title="Spice Girls">Spice Girls</a>' 1996 video, "<a href="/wiki/Wannabe" title="Wannabe">Wannabe</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBradley201014_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBradley201014-123">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Accidents_and_incidents">Accidents and incidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St_Pancras_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Accidents and incidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>On 17 February 1918 a German Gotha aircraft dropped five bombs one of which destroyed the roof of the station's ornate booking hall and killed 20 people. The station was also bombed in World War II, including a <a href="/wiki/Parachute_mine" title="Parachute mine">parachute mine</a> damaging the roof on 15–16 October 1940, and a bomb exploding in the beer vaults underneath Platform 3 on 10–11 May 1941.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJackson198472_34-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJackson198472-34">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 20 July 1959, a locomotive overran a signal and consequently crashed into Dock Junction Signal Box. As a result, trains had to be hand-signalled in and out of St Pancras for several days.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETrevena198142_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETrevena198142-124">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Service_patterns">Service patterns</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St_Pancras_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Service patterns">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Future_developments">Future developments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St_Pancras_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Future developments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Competition_with_Eurostar">Competition with Eurostar</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St_Pancras_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Competition with Eurostar">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/High_Speed_1#Future_operations" title="High Speed 1">High Speed 1 §&#160;Future operations</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:St_Pancras_railway_station_MMB_71_406-585.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/St_Pancras_railway_station_MMB_71_406-585.jpg/220px-St_Pancras_railway_station_MMB_71_406-585.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/St_Pancras_railway_station_MMB_71_406-585.jpg/330px-St_Pancras_railway_station_MMB_71_406-585.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/St_Pancras_railway_station_MMB_71_406-585.jpg/440px-St_Pancras_railway_station_MMB_71_406-585.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3864" data-file-height="2513" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:St_Pancras_railway_station_MMB_71_406-585.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Deutsche Bahn ICE3 train at St Pancras on 19 October 2010</div></div></div>
<p>In January 2010, the European railway network was opened to liberalisation to allow greater competition.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> Both <a href="/wiki/Air_France-KLM" class="mw-redirect" title="Air France-KLM">Air France-KLM</a> and <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Bahn" title="Deutsche Bahn">Deutsche Bahn</a> expressed interest in taking advantage of the new laws to run new services via High Speed 1 to St Pancras.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In December 2009, Deutsche Bahn received permission to run trains through the Channel Tunnel after safety requirements were relaxed.  It had previously expressed a desire to run through trains between London and Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-ES-DB1_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ES-DB1-128">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> Direct trains between St Pancras and <a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a> could have started before the 2012 Olympics,<sup id="cite_ref-ES-DB2_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ES-DB2-131">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> with plans to run a regular service of three daily trains each direction to <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rotterdam" title="Rotterdam">Rotterdam</a> and Amsterdam via Brussels in 2013. Deutsche Bahn trains would be made up of two coupled sets between London and Brussels, dividing at Bruxelles-Midi/Brussel-Zuid. DB showcased an <a href="/wiki/ICE_3" title="ICE 3">ICE 3</a> trainset in St Pancras in October 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> The start date for these services is not expected before 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-irj_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-irj-133">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> In March 2017 it was announced that Deutsche Bahn had revived plans for a London to Frankfurt train service taking 5 hours, with the service beginning as early as 2020,<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> though plans were later shelved.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In February 2010, the idea of a Transmanche Metro service gained support as local councillors in <a href="/wiki/Kent" title="Kent">Kent</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pas-de-Calais" title="Pas-de-Calais">Pas-de-Calais</a> announced that they were in talks to establish a high-frequency stopping service between London and Lille. Trains would start at Lille Europe and call at Calais, Ashford International and Stratford International before reaching St Pancras. Since High Speed 1 opened, Ashford and Calais have an infrequent service and Eurostar trains do not call at Stratford International. It was hoped the service would be running by 2012 in time for the London Olympics.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> The mayor of Calais revived these plans in 2016, and said it could be operational in five years.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Great_Northern">Great Northern</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St_Pancras_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Great Northern">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>From December 2018, as part of the Thameslink programme, services from the East Coast Main Line/<a href="/wiki/Great_Northern_Route" title="Great Northern Route">Great Northern Route</a>, also part of the <a href="/wiki/Govia_Thameslink_Railway" title="Govia Thameslink Railway">Govia Thameslink Railway</a> franchise, will be linked to the Thameslink route, diverting trains previously terminating at Kings Cross into the Thameslink platforms at St Pancras and then through central London to Sussex and Kent.
This link was made possible by the construction of a pair of single-tracks tunnels, named the "canal tunnels". These tunnel start immediately of the St Pancras Thameslink platforms, dive under the <a href="/wiki/Regent%27s_Canal" title="Regent&#39;s Canal">Regent's Canal</a>, and join the <a href="/wiki/East_Coast_Main_Line" title="East Coast Main Line">East Coast Main Line</a> where the <a href="/wiki/North_London_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="North London Line">North London Line</a> and <a href="/wiki/High_Speed_1" title="High Speed 1">High Speed 1</a> pass over the top.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Freight">Freight</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St_Pancras_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Freight">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 21 March 2012, a <a href="/wiki/SNCF_TGV_La_Poste" title="SNCF TGV La Poste">SNCF TGV La Poste</a> trainset was displayed at St Pancras.<sup id="cite_ref-rgi20120321_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rgi20120321-139">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> However, regular services proposed for 2017 would use a new terminal planned near Barking.<sup id="cite_ref-rgi20120321_139-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rgi20120321-139">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Underground">Underground</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St_Pancras_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Underground">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:St_Pancras_railway_station_MMB_G9.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/St_Pancras_railway_station_MMB_G9.jpg/220px-St_Pancras_railway_station_MMB_G9.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/St_Pancras_railway_station_MMB_G9.jpg/330px-St_Pancras_railway_station_MMB_G9.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/St_Pancras_railway_station_MMB_G9.jpg/440px-St_Pancras_railway_station_MMB_G9.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3720" data-file-height="2457" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:St_Pancras_railway_station_MMB_G9.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>One of the entrances to King's Cross St Pancras tube station from the St Pancras concourse.</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/King%27s_Cross_St_Pancras_tube_station" title="King&#39;s Cross St Pancras tube station">King's Cross St Pancras tube station</a></div>
<p>King's Cross St Pancras tube station serves both King's Cross and St Pancras main-line stations. It is in fare zone 1.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> The station has two ticket halls, both of which can be accessed directly from the St Pancras concourse.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> The tube station is served by more lines than any other station on the London Underground. In 2005 &amp; 2017, the tube station was the busiest on the network.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The tube station pre-dated the mainline as part of the initial section of <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Railway" title="Metropolitan Railway">Metropolitan Railway</a> project on 10 January 1863, which was the first section of the London Underground to open.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDayReed200814_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDayReed200814-144">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> The station expanded to accommodate St Pancras on opening, following by interchanges with the Great Northern, Piccadilly and Brompton Railway (now the <a href="/wiki/Piccadilly_line" title="Piccadilly line">Piccadilly line</a>) in 1906,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWolmar2004181_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWolmar2004181-145">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> with the City &amp; South London Railway (now the <a href="/wiki/Northern_line" title="Northern line">Northern line</a>) opening a year later.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDayReed200847_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDayReed200847-146">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Victoria_line" title="Victoria line">Victoria line</a> platforms were opened in 1968.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMenear1983112_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMenear1983112-147">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> A major expansion to accommodate High Speed 1 at St. Pancras opened in November 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A pedestrian <a href="/wiki/Subway_(underpass)" title="Subway (underpass)">subway</a> was built during the CTRL refurbishments.  It runs under Pancras Road from the eastern entrance of the domestic concourse to the new northern ticket hall of King's Cross St Pancras tube station (opened November 2009) and the new concourse for King's Cross (opened March 2012).<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St_Pancras_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-23"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-23">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Beer traffic was handled in the centre of the station between platforms&#160;4 and&#160;5. A central third track ended in a wagon hoist lowering wagons 20&#160;feet (6&#160;m) below rail level. Beer storage ended in 1967.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELambert201058_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELambert201058-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-115"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-115">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Scott had previously submitted Gothic inspired designs for the <a href="/wiki/Foreign_Office" class="mw-redirect" title="Foreign Office">Foreign Office</a>, but had had his designs blocked.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJackson198468_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJackson198468-114">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>
